## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of time and velocity. In nonlinear oscillator theory, the acceleration depends on restoring forces (often functions of displacement, which is related to the integral of velocity) and damping forces (functions of velocity), leading to nonlinear terms in v and potentially periodic functions of t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic drag-like damping)
- Cubic restoring via velocity proxy: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (Duffing-type nonlinearity in velocity)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v (self-sustained oscillation with nonlinear damping)
- Harmonic driving with damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (driven damped oscillator)
- Polynomial restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity)
- Sinusoidal restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (pendulum-like with velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Rayleigh-type with forcing)
- Cosine restoring: dv_dt = c0 * cos(c1 * t) (acceleration from sinusoidal position restoring force)
- Combined harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (superposition of harmonic restoring terms)
- Nonlinear damped driven: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 - v**2) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (limit cycle with driving)
- Position-reconstructed restoring: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (restoring force as function of phase)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (higher-order nonlinear oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Nonlinear restoring force → odd-power polynomials in displacement (v**1, v**3, v**5) preserving symmetry
- Self-excited oscillation → terms of the form (1 - c*v**2)*v indicating amplitude-dependent damping sign change
- Periodic position dependence through time → sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) as proxy for displacement when position is not directly available
- Energy-dependent damping → v**2 * v or |v|*v terms representing velocity-dependent dissipation
- Phase-space structure → acceleration as a function of v alone implies autonomous system; dependence on t implies non-autonomous or that position information is encoded in t
- Frequency mixing in driven systems → products like v*sin(c*t) representing parametric or nonlinear coupling
- Hardening/softening springs → sign of cubic coefficient in v**3 determines whether restoring force stiffens or softens with amplitude
- Limit cycle behavior → balance between negative linear damping (c0*v with c0>0 feeding energy) and cubic dissipation (c1*v**3 with c1<0 removing energy)
